                                 HOUSE FILE 

                                 HOUSE FILE 
                                 HOUSE FILE                                  HOUSE FILE                                  BY  COMMITTEE ON ECONOMIC
                                     GROWTH

                                 (SUCCESSOR TO HSB 518)

 A BILL FOR

  1 An Act relating to the administration of programs by the
  2    economic development authority by creating a renewable
  3    chemical production tax credit program, modifying the high
  4    quality jobs program,  and including effective date and other
  5    applicability provisions.
  6 BE IT ENACTED BY THE GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE STATE OF IOWA:
    TLSB 5172HV (1) 86
    mm/sc

  1 12 July 1, 2021.  1 12 July 1, 2021.  1 13                           DIVISION II
  1 14        RENEWABLE CHEMICAL PRODUCTION TAX CREDIT PROGRAM
  1 15    Sec. 2.  Section 15.119, subsection 2, Code 2016, is amended
  1 16 by adding the following new paragraph:
  1 17      1 14        RENEWABLE CHEMICAL PRODUCTION TAX CREDIT PROGRAM
  1 15    Sec. 2.  Section 15.119, subsection 2, Code 2016, is amended
  1 16 by adding the following new paragraph:
  1 17      1 15    Sec. 2.  Section 15.119, subsection 2, Code 2016, is amended
  1 16 by adding the following new paragraph:
  1 17      1 16 by adding the following new paragraph:
  1 17      1 17      1 18 credit program administered pursuant to sections 15.315 through
  1 19 15.320.  In allocating tax credits pursuant to this subsection,
  1 20 the authority shall not allocate more than ten million dollars
  1 21 for purposes of this paragraph.
  1 22    Sec. 3.    1 19 15.320.  In allocating tax credits pursuant to this subsection,
  1 20 the authority shall not allocate more than ten million dollars
  1 21 for purposes of this paragraph.
  1 22    Sec. 3.    1 20 the authority shall not allocate more than ten million dollars
  1 21 for purposes of this paragraph.
  1 22    Sec. 3.    1 21 for purposes of this paragraph.
  1 22    Sec. 3.    1 22    Sec. 3.    1 23    This part shall be known and may be cited as the "Renewable
  1 24 Chemical Production Tax Credit Program".
  1 25    Sec. 4.    1 24 Chemical Production Tax Credit Program".
  1 25    Sec. 4.    1 25    Sec. 4.    1 26    As used in this part, unless the context otherwise requires:
  1 27    1.  "Biobased content percentage" means, with respect to any
  1 28 renewable chemical, the amount, expressed as a percentage, of
  1 29 renewable organic material present as determined by testing
  1 30 representative samples using the American society for testing
  1 31 and materials standard D6866.
  1 32    2.  "Biomass feedstock" means sugar, polysaccharide,
  1 33 glycerin, lignin, fat, grease, or oil derived from a plant or
  1 34 animal, or a protein capable of being converted to a building
  1 35 block chemical by means of a biological or chemical conversion
  2  1 process.
  2  2    3.  "Building block chemical" means a molecule converted
  2  3 from biomass feedstock as a first product or a secondarily
  2  4 derived product that can be further refined into a higher=value
  2  5 chemical, material, or consumer product. "Building block
  2  6 chemical" includes but is not limited to glycerol, methanoic
  2  7 or formic acid, arabonic acid, erythonic acid, glyceric acid,
  2  8 glycolic acid, lactic acid, 3=hydroxypropionate, propionic
  2  9 acid, malonic acid, serine, succinic acid, fumaric acid,
  2 10 malic acid, aspartic acid, 3=hydroxybutyrolactone, acetoin,
  2 11 threonine, itaconic acid, furfural, levulinic acid, glutamic
  2 12 acid, xylonic acid, xylaric acid, xylitol, arabitol, citric
  2 13 acid, aconitic acid, 5=hydroxymethylfurfural, lysine, gluconic
  2 14 acid, glucaric acid, sorbitol, gallic acid, ferulic acid,
  2 15 nonfuel butanol, nonfuel ethanol, a polymer or gum that can be
  2 16 produced directly from a protein=based biomass feedstock, or
  2 17 such additional molecules as may be included by the authority
  2 18 by rule.
  2 19    4.  "Eligible business" means a business meeting the
  2 20 requirements of section 15.317.
  2 21    5.  "Food additive" means a building block chemical that
  2 22 is not primarily consumed as food but which, when combined
  2 23 with other components, improves the taste, appearance, odor,
  2 24 texture, or nutritional content of food.  The authority, in its
  2 25 discretion, shall determine whether or not a building block
  2 26 chemical is primarily consumed as food.
  2 27    6.  "Program" means the renewable chemical production tax
  2 28 credit program administered pursuant to this part.
  2 29    7.  "Renewable chemical" means a building block chemical
  2 30 with a biobased content percentage of at least fifty percent.
  2 31 "Renewable chemical" does not include a chemical sold or used
  2 32 for the production of food, feed, or fuel. "Renewable chemical"
  2 33 includes cellulosic ethanol, starch ethanol, or other ethanol
  2 34 derived from biomass feedstock, fatty acid methyl esters,
  2 35 or butanol, but only to the extent that such molecules are
  3  1 produced and sold for uses other than food, feed, or fuel.
  3  2 "Renewable chemical" also includes a building block chemical
  3  3 that can be a food additive as long as the building block
  3  4 chemical is not primarily consumed as food and is also sold
  3  5 for uses other than food.  "Renewable chemical" also includes
  3  6 supplements, vitamins, nutraceuticals, and pharmaceuticals, but
  3  7 only to the extent that such molecules do not provide caloric
  3  8 value so as to be considered sustenance as food or feed.
  3  9    8.  "Sugar" means the organic compound glucose, fructose,
  3 10 xylose, arabinose, lactose, sucrose, starch, cellulose, or
  3 11 hemicellulose.
  3 12    Sec. 5.    1 27    1.  "Biobased content percentage" means, with respect to any
  1 28 renewable chemical, the amount, expressed as a percentage, of
  1 29 renewable organic material present as determined by testing
  1 30 representative samples using the American society for testing
  1 31 and materials standard D6866.
  1 32    2.  "Biomass feedstock" means sugar, polysaccharide,

  1 34 animal, or a protein capable of being converted to a building
  1 35 block chemical by means of a biological or chemical conversion
  2  1 process.

  2  3 from biomass feedstock as a first product or a secondarily

  2  5 chemical, material, or consumer product. "Building block
  2  6 chemical" includes but is not limited to glycerol, methanoic

  2 10 malic acid, aspartic acid, 3=hydroxybutyrolactone, acetoin,

  2 12 acid, xylonic acid, xylaric acid, xylitol, arabitol, citric

  2 15 nonfuel butanol, nonfuel ethanol, a polymer or gum that can be
  2 16 produced directly from a protein=based biomass feedstock, or
  2 17 such additional molecules as may be included by the authority
  2 18 by rule.
  2 19    4.  "Eligible business" means a business meeting the
  2 20 requirements of section 15.317.

  2 27    6.  "Program" means the renewable chemical production tax
  2 28 credit program administered pursuant to this part.
  2 29    7.  "Renewable chemical" means a building block chemical
  2 30 with a biobased content percentage of at least fifty percent.
  2 31 "Renewable chemical" does not include a chemical sold or used
  2 32 for the production of food, feed, or fuel. "Renewable chemical"
  2 33 includes cellulosic ethanol, starch ethanol, or other ethanol
  2 34 derived from biomass feedstock, fatty acid methyl esters,
  2 35 or butanol, but only to the extent that such molecules are
  3  1 produced and sold for uses other than food, feed, or fuel.
  3  2 "Renewable chemical" also includes a building block chemical
  3  3 that can be a food additive as long as the building block
  3  4 chemical is not primarily consumed as food and is also sold
  3  5 for uses other than food.  "Renewable chemical" also includes
  3  6 supplements, vitamins, nutraceuticals, and pharmaceuticals, but
  3  7 only to the extent that such molecules do not provide caloric
  3  8 value so as to be considered sustenance as food or feed.
  3  9    8.  "Sugar" means the organic compound glucose, fructose,
  3 10 xylose, arabinose, lactose, sucrose, starch, cellulose, or
  3 11 hemicellulose.

  2  3 from biomass feedstock as a first product or a secondarily
  2  4 derived product that can be further refined into a higher=value

  3  6 supplements, vitamins, nutraceuticals, and pharmaceuticals, but
  3  7 only to the extent that such molecules do not provide caloric
  3  8 value so as to be considered sustenance as food or feed.
  3  9    8.  "Sugar" means the organic compound glucose, fructose,
  3 10 xylose, arabinose, lactose, sucrose, starch, cellulose, or
  3 11 hemicellulose.

  3  6 supplements, vitamins, nutraceuticals, and pharmaceuticals, but
  3  7 only to the extent that such molecules do not provide caloric
  3  8 value so as to be considered sustenance as food or feed.
  3  9    8.  "Sugar" means the organic compound glucose, fructose,
  3 10 xylose, arabinose, lactose, sucrose, starch, cellulose, or
  3 11 hemicellulose.

  3 12    Sec. 5.    3 12    Sec. 5.    3 13    To be eligible to receive the renewable chemical production
  3 14 tax credit pursuant to the program, a business shall meet all
  3 15 of the following requirements:
  3 16    1.  The business is physically located in this state.
  3 17    2.  The business is operated for profit and under single
  3 18 management.
  3 19    3.  The business is not an entity providing professional
  3 20 services, health care services, or medical treatments or an
  3 21 entity engaged primarily in retail operations.
  3 22    4.  The business organized, expanded, or located in the state
  3 23 on or after the effective date of this division of this Act.
  3 24    5.  The business shall not be relocating or reducing
  3 25 operations as described in section 15.329, subsection 1,
  3 26 paragraph "b", and as determined under the discretion of the
  3 27 authority.
  3 28    6.  The business is in compliance with all agreements entered
  3 29 into under this program or other programs administered by the
  3 30 authority.

  3 31    Sec. 6.    3 30 authority.
  3 31    Sec. 6.    3 31    Sec. 6.    3 32 and agreement ==== maximum tax credits.
  3 33    1.  Application.
  3 34    a.  An eligible business that produces a renewable chemical
  3 35 in this state from biomass feedstock during a calendar year may
  4  1 apply to the authority for the renewable chemical production
  4  2 tax credit provided in section 15.319.
  4  3    b.  The application shall be made to the authority in the
  4  4 manner prescribed by the authority.
  4  5    c.  The application shall be made during the calendar year
  4  6 following the calendar year in which the renewable chemicals
  4  7 are produced.
  4  8    d.  The authority may accept applications on a continuous
  4  9 basis or may establish, by rule, an annual application
  4 10 deadline.
  4 11    e.  The application shall include all of the following
  4 12 information:
  4 13    (1)  The amount of renewable chemicals produced in the state
  4 14 from biomass feedstock by the eligible business during the
  4 15 calendar year, measured in pounds.
  4 16    (2)  Any other information reasonably required by the
  4 17 authority in order to establish and verify eligibility under
  4 18 the program.
  4 19    2.  Agreement and fees.
  4 20    a.  Before being issued a tax credit under section 15.319,
  4 21 an eligible business shall enter into an agreement with the
  4 22 authority for the successful completion of all requirements of
  4 23 the program.
  4 24    b.  The compliance cost fees authorized in section 15.330,
  4 25 subsection 12, shall apply to all agreements entered into
  4 26 under this program and shall be collected by the authority in
  4 27 the same manner and to the same extent as described in that
  4 28 subsection.
  4 29    c.  An eligible business shall fulfill all the requirements
  4 30 of the program and the agreement before receiving a tax credit
  4 31 or entering into a subsequent agreement under this section.
  4 32 The authority may decline to enter into a subsequent agreement
  4 33 under this section or issue a tax credit if an agreement is not
  4 34 successfully fulfilled.
  4 35    d.  Upon establishing that all requirements of the program
  5  1 and the agreement have been fulfilled, the authority shall
  5  2 issue a tax credit and related tax credit certificate to the
  5  3 eligible business stating the amount of renewable chemical
  5  4 production tax credit the eligible business may claim.
  5  5    3.  Maximum tax credit amount.
  5  6    a.  The maximum amount of tax credit that may be issued under
  5  7 section 15.319 to an eligible business for the production of
  5  8 renewable chemicals in a calendar year shall not exceed the
  5  9 following:
  5 10    (1)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 11 operation in the state for five years or less at the time of
  5 12 application, one million dollars.
  5 13    (2)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 14 operation in the state for more than five years at the time of
  5 15 application, five hundred thousand dollars.
  5 16    b.  An eligible business shall not receive a tax credit for
  5 17 renewable chemicals produced before the date the business first
  5 18 qualified as an eligible business pursuant to section 15.317.
  5 19    c.  An eligible business shall not receive more than five tax
  5 20 credits under the program.
  5 21    d.  The authority shall issue tax credits under the program
  5 22 on a first=come, first=served basis until the maximum amount of
  5 23 tax credits allocated pursuant to section 15.119, subsection
  5 24 2, paragraph "h", is reached.  The authority shall maintain
  5 25 a list of successful applicants under the program, so that
  5 26 if the maximum aggregate amount of tax credits is reached in
  5 27 a given fiscal year, eligible businesses that successfully
  5 28 applied but for which tax credits were not issued shall be
  5 29 placed on a wait list in the order the eligible businesses
  5 30 applied and shall be given priority for receiving tax credits
  5 31 in succeeding fiscal years. Placement on a wait list pursuant
  5 32 to this paragraph shall not constitute a promise binding the
  5 33 state. The availability of a tax credit and issuance of a tax
  5 34 credit certificate pursuant to this subsection in a future
  5 35 fiscal year is contingent upon the availability of tax credits
  6  1 in that particular fiscal year.
  6  2    4.  Termination and repayment.  The failure by an eligible
  6  3 business in fulfilling any requirement of the program or any of
  6  4 the terms and obligations of an agreement entered into pursuant
  6  5 to this section may result in the reduction, termination,
  6  6 or recision of the tax credits under section 15.319 and may
  6  7 subject the eligible business to the repayment or recapture of
  6  8 tax credits claimed.  The repayment or recapture of tax credits
  6  9 pursuant to this subsection shall be accomplished in the same
  6 10 manner as provided in section 15.330, subsection 2.
  6 11    5.  Confidentiality.
  6 12    a.  Except as provided in paragraph "b", any information
  6 13 or record in the possession of the authority with respect to
  6 14 the program shall be presumed by the authority to be a trade
  6 15 secret protected under chapter 550 or common law and shall be
  6 16 kept confidential by the authority unless otherwise ordered by
  6 17 a court.
  6 18    b.  The identity of a tax credit recipient and the amount
  6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.
  6 21    Sec. 7.    3 33    1.  Application.

  5  6    a.  The maximum amount of tax credit that may be issued under
  5  7 section 15.319 to an eligible business for the production of
  5  8 renewable chemicals in a calendar year shall not exceed the
  5  9 following:
  5 10    (1)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 11 operation in the state for five years or less at the time of
  5 12 application, one million dollars.
  5 13    (2)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 14 operation in the state for more than five years at the time of
  5 15 application, five hundred thousand dollars.
  5 16    b.  An eligible business shall not receive a tax credit for
  5 17 renewable chemicals produced before the date the business first
  5 18 qualified as an eligible business pursuant to section 15.317.
  5 19    c.  An eligible business shall not receive more than five tax
  5 20 credits under the program.
  5 21    d.  The authority shall issue tax credits under the program
  5 22 on a first=come, first=served basis until the maximum amount of
  5 23 tax credits allocated pursuant to section 15.119, subsection
  5 24 2, paragraph "h", is reached.  The authority shall maintain
  5 25 a list of successful applicants under the program, so that
  5 26 if the maximum aggregate amount of tax credits is reached in
  5 27 a given fiscal year, eligible businesses that successfully
  5 28 applied but for which tax credits were not issued shall be
  5 29 placed on a wait list in the order the eligible businesses
  5 30 applied and shall be given priority for receiving tax credits
  5 31 in succeeding fiscal years. Placement on a wait list pursuant
  5 32 to this paragraph shall not constitute a promise binding the
  5 33 state. The availability of a tax credit and issuance of a tax
  5 34 credit certificate pursuant to this subsection in a future
  5 35 fiscal year is contingent upon the availability of tax credits
  6  1 in that particular fiscal year.
  6  2    4.  Termination and repayment.  The failure by an eligible
  6  3 business in fulfilling any requirement of the program or any of
  6  4 the terms and obligations of an agreement entered into pursuant
  6  5 to this section may result in the reduction, termination,
  6  6 or recision of the tax credits under section 15.319 and may
  6  7 subject the eligible business to the repayment or recapture of
  6  8 tax credits claimed.  The repayment or recapture of tax credits
  6  9 pursuant to this subsection shall be accomplished in the same
  6 10 manner as provided in section 15.330, subsection 2.
  6 11    5.  Confidentiality.
  6 12    a.  Except as provided in paragraph "b", any information
  6 13 or record in the possession of the authority with respect to
  6 14 the program shall be presumed by the authority to be a trade
  6 15 secret protected under chapter 550 or common law and shall be
  6 16 kept confidential by the authority unless otherwise ordered by
  6 17 a court.
  6 18    b.  The identity of a tax credit recipient and the amount
  6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.
  6 21    Sec. 7.    4  1 apply to the authority for the renewable chemical production
  4  2 tax credit provided in section 15.319.
  4  3    b.  The application shall be made to the authority in the
  4  4 manner prescribed by the authority.
  4  5    c.  The application shall be made during the calendar year
  4  6 following the calendar year in which the renewable chemicals
  4  7 are produced.
  4  8    d.  The authority may accept applications on a continuous
  4  9 basis or may establish, by rule, an annual application
  4 10 deadline.
  4 11    e.  The application shall include all of the following
  4 12 information:
  4 13    (1)  The amount of renewable chemicals produced in the state
  4 14 from biomass feedstock by the eligible business during the
  4 15 calendar year, measured in pounds.
  4 16    (2)  Any other information reasonably required by the
  4 17 authority in order to establish and verify eligibility under
  4 18 the program.
  4 19    2.  Agreement and fees.
  4 20    a.  Before being issued a tax credit under section 15.319,
  4 21 an eligible business shall enter into an agreement with the
  4 22 authority for the successful completion of all requirements of
  4 23 the program.
  4 24    b.  The compliance cost fees authorized in section 15.330,
  4 25 subsection 12, shall apply to all agreements entered into
  4 26 under this program and shall be collected by the authority in
  4 27 the same manner and to the same extent as described in that
  4 28 subsection.
  4 29    c.  An eligible business shall fulfill all the requirements
  4 30 of the program and the agreement before receiving a tax credit
  4 31 or entering into a subsequent agreement under this section.
  4 32 The authority may decline to enter into a subsequent agreement
  4 33 under this section or issue a tax credit if an agreement is not
  4 34 successfully fulfilled.
  4 35    d.  Upon establishing that all requirements of the program
  5  1 and the agreement have been fulfilled, the authority shall
  5  2 issue a tax credit and related tax credit certificate to the
  5  3 eligible business stating the amount of renewable chemical
  5  4 production tax credit the eligible business may claim.
  5  5    3.  Maximum tax credit amount.
  5  6    a.  The maximum amount of tax credit that may be issued under

  5  4 production tax credit the eligible business may claim.
  5  5    3.  Maximum tax credit amount.
  5  6    a.  The maximum amount of tax credit that may be issued under
  5  7 section 15.319 to an eligible business for the production of
  5  8 renewable chemicals in a calendar year shall not exceed the
  5  9 following:
  5 10    (1)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 11 operation in the state for five years or less at the time of
  5 12 application, one million dollars.
  5 13    (2)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 14 operation in the state for more than five years at the time of
  5 15 application, five hundred thousand dollars.
  5 16    b.  An eligible business shall not receive a tax credit for
  5 17 renewable chemicals produced before the date the business first
  5 18 qualified as an eligible business pursuant to section 15.317.
  5 19    c.  An eligible business shall not receive more than five tax
  5 20 credits under the program.
  5 21    d.  The authority shall issue tax credits under the program
  5 22 on a first=come, first=served basis until the maximum amount of
  5 23 tax credits allocated pursuant to section 15.119, subsection
  5 24 2, paragraph "h", is reached.  The authority shall maintain
  5 25 a list of successful applicants under the program, so that
  5 26 if the maximum aggregate amount of tax credits is reached in
  5 27 a given fiscal year, eligible businesses that successfully
  5 28 applied but for which tax credits were not issued shall be
  5 29 placed on a wait list in the order the eligible businesses
  5 30 applied and shall be given priority for receiving tax credits
  5 31 in succeeding fiscal years. Placement on a wait list pursuant
  5 32 to this paragraph shall not constitute a promise binding the
  5 33 state. The availability of a tax credit and issuance of a tax
  5 34 credit certificate pursuant to this subsection in a future
  5 35 fiscal year is contingent upon the availability of tax credits
  6  1 in that particular fiscal year.
  6  2    4.  Termination and repayment.  The failure by an eligible
  6  3 business in fulfilling any requirement of the program or any of
  6  4 the terms and obligations of an agreement entered into pursuant
  6  5 to this section may result in the reduction, termination,
  6  6 or recision of the tax credits under section 15.319 and may
  6  7 subject the eligible business to the repayment or recapture of
  6  8 tax credits claimed.  The repayment or recapture of tax credits
  6  9 pursuant to this subsection shall be accomplished in the same
  6 10 manner as provided in section 15.330, subsection 2.
  6 11    5.  Confidentiality.
  6 12    a.  Except as provided in paragraph "b", any information
  6 13 or record in the possession of the authority with respect to
  6 14 the program shall be presumed by the authority to be a trade
  6 15 secret protected under chapter 550 or common law and shall be
  6 16 kept confidential by the authority unless otherwise ordered by
  6 17 a court.
  6 18    b.  The identity of a tax credit recipient and the amount
  6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.
  6 21    Sec. 7.    4  7 are produced.
  4  8    d.  The authority may accept applications on a continuous
  4  9 basis or may establish, by rule, an annual application
  4 10 deadline.
  4 11    e.  The application shall include all of the following
  4 12 information:
  4 13    (1)  The amount of renewable chemicals produced in the state
  4 14 from biomass feedstock by the eligible business during the
  4 15 calendar year, measured in pounds.
  4 16    (2)  Any other information reasonably required by the
  4 17 authority in order to establish and verify eligibility under
  4 18 the program.
  4 19    2.  Agreement and fees.
  4 20    a.  Before being issued a tax credit under section 15.319,
  4 21 an eligible business shall enter into an agreement with the
  4 22 authority for the successful completion of all requirements of
  4 23 the program.
  4 24    b.  The compliance cost fees authorized in section 15.330,
  4 25 subsection 12, shall apply to all agreements entered into
  4 26 under this program and shall be collected by the authority in
  4 27 the same manner and to the same extent as described in that
  4 28 subsection.
  4 29    c.  An eligible business shall fulfill all the requirements
  4 30 of the program and the agreement before receiving a tax credit
  4 31 or entering into a subsequent agreement under this section.
  4 32 The authority may decline to enter into a subsequent agreement
  4 33 under this section or issue a tax credit if an agreement is not
  4 34 successfully fulfilled.
  4 35    d.  Upon establishing that all requirements of the program
  5  1 and the agreement have been fulfilled, the authority shall
  5  2 issue a tax credit and related tax credit certificate to the
  5  3 eligible business stating the amount of renewable chemical
  5  4 production tax credit the eligible business may claim.

  5 35 fiscal year is contingent upon the availability of tax credits
  6  1 in that particular fiscal year.
  6  2    4.  Termination and repayment.  The failure by an eligible
  6  3 business in fulfilling any requirement of the program or any of
  6  4 the terms and obligations of an agreement entered into pursuant
  6  5 to this section may result in the reduction, termination,
  6  6 or recision of the tax credits under section 15.319 and may
  6  7 subject the eligible business to the repayment or recapture of
  6  8 tax credits claimed.  The repayment or recapture of tax credits
  6  9 pursuant to this subsection shall be accomplished in the same
  6 10 manner as provided in section 15.330, subsection 2.
  6 11    5.  Confidentiality.
  6 12    a.  Except as provided in paragraph "b", any information
  6 13 or record in the possession of the authority with respect to
  6 14 the program shall be presumed by the authority to be a trade
  6 15 secret protected under chapter 550 or common law and shall be
  6 16 kept confidential by the authority unless otherwise ordered by
  6 17 a court.
  6 18    b.  The identity of a tax credit recipient and the amount
  6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.
  6 21    Sec. 7.    4 13    (1)  The amount of renewable chemicals produced in the state
  4 14 from biomass feedstock by the eligible business during the
  4 15 calendar year, measured in pounds.
  4 16    (2)  Any other information reasonably required by the
  4 17 authority in order to establish and verify eligibility under
  4 18 the program.
  4 19    2.  Agreement and fees.
  4 20    a.  Before being issued a tax credit under section 15.319,
  4 21 an eligible business shall enter into an agreement with the
  4 22 authority for the successful completion of all requirements of
  4 23 the program.
  4 24    b.  The compliance cost fees authorized in section 15.330,
  4 25 subsection 12, shall apply to all agreements entered into
  4 26 under this program and shall be collected by the authority in
  4 27 the same manner and to the same extent as described in that
  4 28 subsection.
  4 29    c.  An eligible business shall fulfill all the requirements
  4 30 of the program and the agreement before receiving a tax credit
  4 31 or entering into a subsequent agreement under this section.
  4 32 The authority may decline to enter into a subsequent agreement
  4 33 under this section or issue a tax credit if an agreement is not
  4 34 successfully fulfilled.
  4 35    d.  Upon establishing that all requirements of the program
  5  1 and the agreement have been fulfilled, the authority shall
  5  2 issue a tax credit and related tax credit certificate to the
  5  3 eligible business stating the amount of renewable chemical
  5  4 production tax credit the eligible business may claim.
  5  5    3.  Maximum tax credit amount.
  5  6    a.  The maximum amount of tax credit that may be issued under
  5  7 section 15.319 to an eligible business for the production of
  5  8 renewable chemicals in a calendar year shall not exceed the
  5  9 following:
  5 10    (1)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 11 operation in the state for five years or less at the time of
  5 12 application, one million dollars.
  5 13    (2)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 14 operation in the state for more than five years at the time of
  5 15 application, five hundred thousand dollars.
  5 16    b.  An eligible business shall not receive a tax credit for
  5 17 renewable chemicals produced before the date the business first
  5 18 qualified as an eligible business pursuant to section 15.317.
  5 19    c.  An eligible business shall not receive more than five tax
  5 20 credits under the program.
  5 21    d.  The authority shall issue tax credits under the program
  5 22 on a first=come, first=served basis until the maximum amount of
  5 23 tax credits allocated pursuant to section 15.119, subsection
  5 24 2, paragraph "h", is reached.  The authority shall maintain
  5 25 a list of successful applicants under the program, so that
  5 26 if the maximum aggregate amount of tax credits is reached in
  5 27 a given fiscal year, eligible businesses that successfully
  5 28 applied but for which tax credits were not issued shall be
  5 29 placed on a wait list in the order the eligible businesses
  5 30 applied and shall be given priority for receiving tax credits
  5 31 in succeeding fiscal years. Placement on a wait list pursuant
  5 32 to this paragraph shall not constitute a promise binding the
  5 33 state. The availability of a tax credit and issuance of a tax
  5 34 credit certificate pursuant to this subsection in a future
  5 35 fiscal year is contingent upon the availability of tax credits
  6  1 in that particular fiscal year.
  6  2    4.  Termination and repayment.  The failure by an eligible

  5 25 a list of successful applicants under the program, so that
  5 26 if the maximum aggregate amount of tax credits is reached in
  5 27 a given fiscal year, eligible businesses that successfully
  5 28 applied but for which tax credits were not issued shall be
  5 29 placed on a wait list in the order the eligible businesses
  5 30 applied and shall be given priority for receiving tax credits
  5 31 in succeeding fiscal years. Placement on a wait list pursuant
  5 32 to this paragraph shall not constitute a promise binding the
  5 33 state. The availability of a tax credit and issuance of a tax
  5 34 credit certificate pursuant to this subsection in a future
  5 35 fiscal year is contingent upon the availability of tax credits
  6  1 in that particular fiscal year.
  6  2    4.  Termination and repayment.  The failure by an eligible
  6  3 business in fulfilling any requirement of the program or any of
  6  4 the terms and obligations of an agreement entered into pursuant
  6  5 to this section may result in the reduction, termination,
  6  6 or recision of the tax credits under section 15.319 and may
  6  7 subject the eligible business to the repayment or recapture of
  6  8 tax credits claimed.  The repayment or recapture of tax credits
  6  9 pursuant to this subsection shall be accomplished in the same
  6 10 manner as provided in section 15.330, subsection 2.
  6 11    5.  Confidentiality.
  6 12    a.  Except as provided in paragraph "b", any information
  6 13 or record in the possession of the authority with respect to
  6 14 the program shall be presumed by the authority to be a trade
  6 15 secret protected under chapter 550 or common law and shall be
  6 16 kept confidential by the authority unless otherwise ordered by
  6 17 a court.
  6 18    b.  The identity of a tax credit recipient and the amount
  6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.
  6 21    Sec. 7.    4 20    a.  Before being issued a tax credit under section 15.319,
  4 21 an eligible business shall enter into an agreement with the
  4 22 authority for the successful completion of all requirements of
  4 23 the program.
  4 24    b.  The compliance cost fees authorized in section 15.330,
  4 25 subsection 12, shall apply to all agreements entered into
  4 26 under this program and shall be collected by the authority in
  4 27 the same manner and to the same extent as described in that
  4 28 subsection.
  4 29    c.  An eligible business shall fulfill all the requirements
  4 30 of the program and the agreement before receiving a tax credit
  4 31 or entering into a subsequent agreement under this section.
  4 32 The authority may decline to enter into a subsequent agreement
  4 33 under this section or issue a tax credit if an agreement is not
  4 34 successfully fulfilled.
  4 35    d.  Upon establishing that all requirements of the program
  5  1 and the agreement have been fulfilled, the authority shall
  5  2 issue a tax credit and related tax credit certificate to the
  5  3 eligible business stating the amount of renewable chemical
  5  4 production tax credit the eligible business may claim.
  5  5    3.  Maximum tax credit amount.
  5  6    a.  The maximum amount of tax credit that may be issued under
  5  7 section 15.319 to an eligible business for the production of
  5  8 renewable chemicals in a calendar year shall not exceed the
  5  9 following:
  5 10    (1)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 11 operation in the state for five years or less at the time of
  5 12 application, one million dollars.
  5 13    (2)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 14 operation in the state for more than five years at the time of
  5 15 application, five hundred thousand dollars.
  5 16    b.  An eligible business shall not receive a tax credit for
  5 17 renewable chemicals produced before the date the business first
  5 18 qualified as an eligible business pursuant to section 15.317.
  5 19    c.  An eligible business shall not receive more than five tax
  5 20 credits under the program.
  5 21    d.  The authority shall issue tax credits under the program
  5 22 on a first=come, first=served basis until the maximum amount of
  5 23 tax credits allocated pursuant to section 15.119, subsection
  5 24 2, paragraph "h", is reached.  The authority shall maintain
  5 25 a list of successful applicants under the program, so that
  5 26 if the maximum aggregate amount of tax credits is reached in
  5 27 a given fiscal year, eligible businesses that successfully
  5 28 applied but for which tax credits were not issued shall be
  5 29 placed on a wait list in the order the eligible businesses
  5 30 applied and shall be given priority for receiving tax credits
  5 31 in succeeding fiscal years. Placement on a wait list pursuant
  5 32 to this paragraph shall not constitute a promise binding the
  5 33 state. The availability of a tax credit and issuance of a tax
  5 34 credit certificate pursuant to this subsection in a future
  5 35 fiscal year is contingent upon the availability of tax credits
  6  1 in that particular fiscal year.
  6  2    4.  Termination and repayment.  The failure by an eligible
  6  3 business in fulfilling any requirement of the program or any of
  6  4 the terms and obligations of an agreement entered into pursuant
  6  5 to this section may result in the reduction, termination,

  4 31 or entering into a subsequent agreement under this section.
  4 32 The authority may decline to enter into a subsequent agreement
  4 33 under this section or issue a tax credit if an agreement is not
  4 34 successfully fulfilled.
  4 35    d.  Upon establishing that all requirements of the program
  5  1 and the agreement have been fulfilled, the authority shall
  5  2 issue a tax credit and related tax credit certificate to the
  5  3 eligible business stating the amount of renewable chemical
  5  4 production tax credit the eligible business may claim.
  5  5    3.  Maximum tax credit amount.
  5  6    a.  The maximum amount of tax credit that may be issued under
  5  7 section 15.319 to an eligible business for the production of
  5  8 renewable chemicals in a calendar year shall not exceed the
  5  9 following:
  5 10    (1)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 11 operation in the state for five years or less at the time of
  5 12 application, one million dollars.
  5 13    (2)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 14 operation in the state for more than five years at the time of
  5 15 application, five hundred thousand dollars.
  5 16    b.  An eligible business shall not receive a tax credit for
  5 17 renewable chemicals produced before the date the business first
  5 18 qualified as an eligible business pursuant to section 15.317.
  5 19    c.  An eligible business shall not receive more than five tax
  5 20 credits under the program.
  5 21    d.  The authority shall issue tax credits under the program
  5 22 on a first=come, first=served basis until the maximum amount of
  5 23 tax credits allocated pursuant to section 15.119, subsection
  5 24 2, paragraph "h", is reached.  The authority shall maintain
  5 25 a list of successful applicants under the program, so that
  5 26 if the maximum aggregate amount of tax credits is reached in
  5 27 a given fiscal year, eligible businesses that successfully
  5 28 applied but for which tax credits were not issued shall be
  5 29 placed on a wait list in the order the eligible businesses
  5 30 applied and shall be given priority for receiving tax credits
  5 31 in succeeding fiscal years. Placement on a wait list pursuant
  5 32 to this paragraph shall not constitute a promise binding the
  5 33 state. The availability of a tax credit and issuance of a tax
  5 34 credit certificate pursuant to this subsection in a future
  5 35 fiscal year is contingent upon the availability of tax credits
  6  1 in that particular fiscal year.
  6  2    4.  Termination and repayment.  The failure by an eligible
  6  3 business in fulfilling any requirement of the program or any of
  6  4 the terms and obligations of an agreement entered into pursuant
  6  5 to this section may result in the reduction, termination,
  6  6 or recision of the tax credits under section 15.319 and may
  6  7 subject the eligible business to the repayment or recapture of
  6  8 tax credits claimed.  The repayment or recapture of tax credits
  6  9 pursuant to this subsection shall be accomplished in the same
  6 10 manner as provided in section 15.330, subsection 2.
  6 11    5.  Confidentiality.
  6 12    a.  Except as provided in paragraph "b", any information
  6 13 or record in the possession of the authority with respect to
  6 14 the program shall be presumed by the authority to be a trade
  6 15 secret protected under chapter 550 or common law and shall be
  6 16 kept confidential by the authority unless otherwise ordered by
  6 17 a court.
  6 18    b.  The identity of a tax credit recipient and the amount
  6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.
  6 21    Sec. 7.    4 28 subsection.

  5 25 a list of successful applicants under the program, so that
  5 26 if the maximum aggregate amount of tax credits is reached in
  5 27 a given fiscal year, eligible businesses that successfully
  5 28 applied but for which tax credits were not issued shall be
  5 29 placed on a wait list in the order the eligible businesses
  5 30 applied and shall be given priority for receiving tax credits
  5 31 in succeeding fiscal years. Placement on a wait list pursuant
  5 32 to this paragraph shall not constitute a promise binding the
  5 33 state. The availability of a tax credit and issuance of a tax
  5 34 credit certificate pursuant to this subsection in a future
  5 35 fiscal year is contingent upon the availability of tax credits
  6  1 in that particular fiscal year.
  6  2    4.  Termination and repayment.  The failure by an eligible
  6  3 business in fulfilling any requirement of the program or any of
  6  4 the terms and obligations of an agreement entered into pursuant
  6  5 to this section may result in the reduction, termination,
  6  6 or recision of the tax credits under section 15.319 and may
  6  7 subject the eligible business to the repayment or recapture of
  6  8 tax credits claimed.  The repayment or recapture of tax credits
  6  9 pursuant to this subsection shall be accomplished in the same
  6 10 manner as provided in section 15.330, subsection 2.
  6 11    5.  Confidentiality.
  6 12    a.  Except as provided in paragraph "b", any information
  6 13 or record in the possession of the authority with respect to
  6 14 the program shall be presumed by the authority to be a trade
  6 15 secret protected under chapter 550 or common law and shall be
  6 16 kept confidential by the authority unless otherwise ordered by
  6 17 a court.
  6 18    b.  The identity of a tax credit recipient and the amount
  6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.
  6 21    Sec. 7.    5  1 and the agreement have been fulfilled, the authority shall
  5  2 issue a tax credit and related tax credit certificate to the
  5  3 eligible business stating the amount of renewable chemical
  5  4 production tax credit the eligible business may claim.
  5  5    3.  Maximum tax credit amount.
  5  6    a.  The maximum amount of tax credit that may be issued under
  5  7 section 15.319 to an eligible business for the production of
  5  8 renewable chemicals in a calendar year shall not exceed the
  5  9 following:
  5 10    (1)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 11 operation in the state for five years or less at the time of
  5 12 application, one million dollars.
  5 13    (2)  In the case of an eligible business that has been in
  5 14 operation in the state for more than five years at the time of
  5 15 application, five hundred thousand dollars.
  5 16    b.  An eligible business shall not receive a tax credit for
  5 17 renewable chemicals produced before the date the business first
  5 18 qualified as an eligible business pursuant to section 15.317.
  5 19    c.  An eligible business shall not receive more than five tax
  5 20 credits under the program.

  5 21    d.  The authority shall issue tax credits under the program
  5 22 on a first=come, first=served basis until the maximum amount of
  5 23 tax credits allocated pursuant to section 15.119, subsection
  5 24 2, paragraph "h", is reached.  The authority shall maintain
  5 25 a list of successful applicants under the program, so that
  5 26 if the maximum aggregate amount of tax credits is reached in
  5 27 a given fiscal year, eligible businesses that successfully
  5 28 applied but for which tax credits were not issued shall be
  5 29 placed on a wait list in the order the eligible businesses
  5 30 applied and shall be given priority for receiving tax credits
  5 31 in succeeding fiscal years. Placement on a wait list pursuant
  5 32 to this paragraph shall not constitute a promise binding the
  5 33 state. The availability of a tax credit and issuance of a tax
  5 34 credit certificate pursuant to this subsection in a future
  5 35 fiscal year is contingent upon the availability of tax credits
  6  1 in that particular fiscal year.
  6  2    4.  Termination and repayment.  The failure by an eligible
  6  3 business in fulfilling any requirement of the program or any of
  6  4 the terms and obligations of an agreement entered into pursuant
  6  5 to this section may result in the reduction, termination,
  6  6 or recision of the tax credits under section 15.319 and may
  6  7 subject the eligible business to the repayment or recapture of
  6  8 tax credits claimed.  The repayment or recapture of tax credits
  6  9 pursuant to this subsection shall be accomplished in the same
  6 10 manner as provided in section 15.330, subsection 2.
  6 11    5.  Confidentiality.
  6 12    a.  Except as provided in paragraph "b", any information
  6 13 or record in the possession of the authority with respect to
  6 14 the program shall be presumed by the authority to be a trade
  6 15 secret protected under chapter 550 or common law and shall be
  6 16 kept confidential by the authority unless otherwise ordered by
  6 17 a court.
  6 18    b.  The identity of a tax credit recipient and the amount
  6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.

  6 12    a.  Except as provided in paragraph "b", any information
  6 13 or record in the possession of the authority with respect to
  6 14 the program shall be presumed by the authority to be a trade
  6 15 secret protected under chapter 550 or common law and shall be
  6 16 kept confidential by the authority unless otherwise ordered by
  6 17 a court.
  6 18    b.  The identity of a tax credit recipient and the amount
  6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.
  6 21    Sec. 7.    5 23 tax credits allocated pursuant to section 15.119, subsection
  5 24 2, paragraph "h", is reached.  The authority shall maintain
  5 25 a list of successful applicants under the program, so that
  5 26 if the maximum aggregate amount of tax credits is reached in
  5 27 a given fiscal year, eligible businesses that successfully
  5 28 applied but for which tax credits were not issued shall be
  5 29 placed on a wait list in the order the eligible businesses
  5 30 applied and shall be given priority for receiving tax credits
  5 31 in succeeding fiscal years. Placement on a wait list pursuant
  5 32 to this paragraph shall not constitute a promise binding the
  5 33 state. The availability of a tax credit and issuance of a tax
  5 34 credit certificate pursuant to this subsection in a future
  5 35 fiscal year is contingent upon the availability of tax credits
  6  1 in that particular fiscal year.
  6  2    4.  Termination and repayment.  The failure by an eligible
  6  3 business in fulfilling any requirement of the program or any of
  6  4 the terms and obligations of an agreement entered into pursuant
  6  5 to this section may result in the reduction, termination,
  6  6 or recision of the tax credits under section 15.319 and may
  6  7 subject the eligible business to the repayment or recapture of
  6  8 tax credits claimed.  The repayment or recapture of tax credits
  6  9 pursuant to this subsection shall be accomplished in the same
  6 10 manner as provided in section 15.330, subsection 2.

  6 21    Sec. 7.    6 10 manner as provided in section 15.330, subsection 2.
  6 11    5.  Confidentiality.
  6 12    a.  Except as provided in paragraph "b", any information
  6 13 or record in the possession of the authority with respect to
  6 14 the program shall be presumed by the authority to be a trade
  6 15 secret protected under chapter 550 or common law and shall be
  6 16 kept confidential by the authority unless otherwise ordered by
  6 17 a court.
  6 18    b.  The identity of a tax credit recipient and the amount
  6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.

  6 21    Sec. 7.    6 18    b.  The identity of a tax credit recipient and the amount
  6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.
  6 21    Sec. 7.    6 19 of the tax credit shall be considered public information under
  6 20 chapter 22.
  6 21    Sec. 7.    6 20 chapter 22.
  6 21    Sec. 7.    6 21    Sec. 7.    6 22 tax credit.
  6 23    1.  An eligible business that has entered into an agreement
  6 24 pursuant to section 15.318 may claim a tax credit in an amount
  6 25 equal to the product of five cents multiplied by the number
  6 26 of pounds of renewable chemicals produced in this state from
  6 27 biomass feedstock by the eligible business during the calendar
  6 28 year. However, an eligible business shall not receive a tax
  6 29 credit for the production of a secondarily derived building
  6 30 block chemical if that chemical is also the subject of a credit
  6 31 at the time of production as a first product. The renewable
  6 32 chemical production tax credit shall not be available for any
  6 33 renewable chemical produced before the 2017 calendar year or
  6 34 after the 2027 calendar year.
  6 35    2.  The tax credit shall be allowed against taxes imposed
  7  1 under chapter 422, division II or III.
  7  2    3.  The tax credit shall be claimed for the tax year during
  7  3 which the eligible business was issued the tax credit.
  7  4    4.  An individual may claim a tax credit under this section
  7  5 of a partnership, limited liability company, S corporation,
  7  6 cooperative organized under chapter 501 and filing as a
  7  7 partnership for federal tax purposes, estate, or trust electing
  7  8 to have income taxed directly to the individual. The amount
  7  9 claimed by the individual shall be based upon the pro rata
  7 10 share of the individual's earnings from the partnership,
  7 11 limited liability company, S corporation, cooperative, estate,
  7 12 or trust.
  7 13    5.  Any tax credit in excess of the tax liability is
  7 14 refundable.  In lieu of claiming a refund, the taxpayer
  7 15 may elect to have the overpayment shown on the taxpayer's
  7 16 final, completed return credited to the tax liability for the
  7 17 following tax year.
  7 18    6.  a.  To claim a tax credit under this section, a taxpayer
  7 19 shall include one or more tax credit certificates with the
  7 20 taxpayer's tax return.
  7 21    b.  The tax credit certificate shall contain the taxpayer's
  7 22 name, address, tax identification number, the amount of the
  7 23 credit, the name of the eligible business, and any other
  7 24 information required by the department of revenue.
  7 25    c.  The tax credit certificate, unless rescinded by the
  7 26 authority, shall be accepted by the department of revenue as
  7 27 payment for taxes imposed pursuant to chapter 422, divisions II
  7 28 and III, subject to any conditions or restrictions placed by
  7 29 the authority upon the face of the tax credit certificate and
  7 30 subject to the limitations of the program.
  7 31    d.  Tax credit certificates issued pursuant to this section
  7 32 shall not be transferred to any other person.
  7 33    Sec. 8.    6 23    1.  An eligible business that has entered into an agreement

  7 23 credit, the name of the eligible business, and any other
  7 24 information required by the department of revenue.
  7 25    c.  The tax credit certificate, unless rescinded by the
  7 26 authority, shall be accepted by the department of revenue as
  7 27 payment for taxes imposed pursuant to chapter 422, divisions II
  7 28 and III, subject to any conditions or restrictions placed by
  7 29 the authority upon the face of the tax credit certificate and
  7 30 subject to the limitations of the program.
  7 31    d.  Tax credit certificates issued pursuant to this section
  7 32 shall not be transferred to any other person.
  7 33    Sec. 8.    6 33 renewable chemical produced before the 2017 calendar year or
  6 34 after the 2027 calendar year.
  6 35    2.  The tax credit shall be allowed against taxes imposed
  7  1 under chapter 422, division II or III.
  7  2    3.  The tax credit shall be claimed for the tax year during
  7  3 which the eligible business was issued the tax credit.
  7  4    4.  An individual may claim a tax credit under this section
  7  5 of a partnership, limited liability company, S corporation,
  7  6 cooperative organized under chapter 501 and filing as a
  7  7 partnership for federal tax purposes, estate, or trust electing
  7  8 to have income taxed directly to the individual. The amount
  7  9 claimed by the individual shall be based upon the pro rata
  7 10 share of the individual's earnings from the partnership,
  7 11 limited liability company, S corporation, cooperative, estate,
  7 12 or trust.

  7 14 refundable.  In lieu of claiming a refund, the taxpayer
  7 15 may elect to have the overpayment shown on the taxpayer's
  7 16 final, completed return credited to the tax liability for the
  7 17 following tax year.

  8 12    Sec. 11.  TAX CREDIT CLAIMS.  Renewable chemical production
  8 13 tax credits issued pursuant to the renewable chemical
  8 14 production tax credit program enacted in this division of this
  8 15 Act shall not be issued by the economic development authority
  8 16 prior to July 1, 2018, and shall not be claimed by a taxpayer
  8 17 prior to September 1, 2018.
  8 18    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  8 19 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  8 20 enactment.
  8 21    Sec. 13.  APPLICABILITY.  This division of this Act applies
  8 22 to renewable chemicals produced in the state from biomass
  8 23 feedstock on or after January 1, 2017.
  8 24                           EXPLANATION
  8 25 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 26 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 27    This bill relates to the administration of programs by
  8 28 the economic development authority (EDA) by modifying the
  8 29 high quality jobs program and creating a renewable chemical
  8 30 production tax credit program.
  8 31    DIVISION I ==== HIGH QUALITY JOBS PROGRAM.  Division I limits
  8 32 for a period of five fiscal years the amount of tax credits
  8 33 that may be allocated to the high quality jobs program, which
  8 34 under current law is subject to EDA's maximum aggregate tax
  8 35 credit cap of $170 million per fiscal year in Code section
  9  1 15.119.  The bill provides that for each of the five fiscal
  9  2 years beginning on July 1, 2016, and ending on June 30, 2021,
  9  3 the authority shall not allocate more than $105 million of
  9  4 that $170 million cap to the high quality jobs program.  This
  9  5 provision is repealed July 1, 2021.
  9  6    DIVISION II ==== RENEWABLE CHEMICAL PRODUCTION TAX CREDIT.
  9  7   Division II creates a renewable chemical production tax credit
  9  8 program (program) that will be administered by the EDA and that
  9  9 will provide tax credits to eligible businesses that produce
  9 10 renewable chemicals in Iowa from biomass feedstock.  "Renewable
  9 11 chemical", "biomass feedstock", and other related terms are
  9 12 defined in the division.
  9 13    In order to qualify for the tax credit, a business must
  9 14 meet several requirements.  First, the business must be
  9 15 physically located in Iowa and operated for profit under
  9 16 single management.  Second, the business must not be an
  9 17 entity providing professional services, health care services,
  9 18 or medical treatments, or be engaged primarily in retail
  9 19 operations.  Third, the business must have organized, expanded,
  9 20 or located in Iowa on or after the effective date of the
  9 21 division.  Fourth, the business must not be, in the discretion
  9 22 of the EDA, ineligible under certain provisions relating to the
  9 23 relocation or reduction of business operations within Iowa.
  9 24 Fifth, the business must be in compliance with all agreements
  9 25 entered into under the program or other programs administered
  9 26 by the EDA.
  9 27    An eligible business seeking a tax credit is required to
  9 28 submit an application to the EDA containing various information
  9 29 during the calendar year following the calendar year in which
  9 30 the renewable chemicals are produced. The EDA may accept
  9 31 applications on a continuous basis or may establish an annual
  9 32 application deadline.
  9 33    Before being issued a tax credit, an eligible business
  9 34 is required to enter into an agreement with the EDA for the
  9 35 successful completion of all requirements of the program.  The
 10  1 EDA is authorized to impose two compliance cost fees under the
 10  2 program.  The first fee equals $500 per agreement.  The second
 10  3 fee equals 0.5 percent of the value of the tax credit claimed
 10  4 pursuant to the agreement if the agreement has an aggregate tax
 10  5 credit value of $100,000 or greater.
 10  6    An eligible business that fails to comply with the
 10  7 requirements of the program or the terms of an agreement with
 10  8 the EDA may have its tax credits reduced, terminated, or
 10  9 rescinded, and may be subject to the repayment or recapture of
 10 10 claimed tax credits.
 10 11    The tax credit equals the product of $.05 multiplied by the
 10 12 number of pounds of renewable chemicals produced in Iowa from
 10 13 biomass feedstock by the eligible business during the calendar
 10 14 year.  Renewable chemicals produced by an eligible business
 10 15 either prior to calendar year 2017 or prior to the date the
 10 16 business first qualifies as an eligible business, or after
 10 17 calendar year 2027, shall not qualify for the tax credit.
 10 18    The tax credit shall be claimed for the tax year during which
 10 19 the eligible business was issued the tax credit.  However, tax
 10 20 credits shall not be issued by EDA prior to July 1, 2018, or
 10 21 claimed by the taxpayer prior to September 1, 2018. The tax
 10 22 credit may be claimed against the individual income tax and the
 10 23 corporate income tax.  The credit is refundable or may, at the
 10 24 election of the taxpayer, be carried forward for up to one tax
 10 25 year.   The tax credit shall not be transferred to any person.
 10 26    The division provides that the program is subject to EDA's
 10 27 maximum aggregate tax credit cap of $170 million per fiscal
 10 28 year in Code section 15.119, and not more than $10 million
 10 29 per fiscal year may be issued by the EDA under the program.
 10 30 In addition, the maximum amount of tax credit that may be
 10 31 issued to an eligible business for the production of renewable
 10 32 chemicals in any one calendar year shall not exceed $1 million
 10 33 or $500,000, depending on whether the eligible business has
 10 34 been operating in Iowa at the time of application for five
 10 35 or fewer years, or more than five years, respectively.  An
 11  1 eligible business shall not receive more than five tax credits
 11  2 under the program.  The EDA is required to issue tax credits
 11  3 on a first=come, first=served basis until the maximum amount
 11  4 of $10 million per fiscal year is reached.  If the amount of
 11  5 tax credits exceeds this amount in a fiscal year, the EDA
 11  6 is required to establish a wait list and give priority in
 11  7 subsequent years to the eligible businesses on the wait list.
 11  8    The division provides for the confidentiality of certain
 11  9 information under the program.  The identity of a tax credit
 11 10 recipient and the amount of the tax credit shall be considered
 11 11 public information under Code chapter 22 (examination of public
 11 12 records), but any other information or record in the possession
 11 13 of the EDA with respect to the program shall be presumed by
 11 14 the EDA to be a trade secret protected under Code chapter 550
 11 15 or common law and shall be kept confidential by the EDA unless
 11 16 otherwise ordered by a court.
 11 17    The division takes effect upon enactment and applies to
 11 18 renewable chemicals produced in Iowa from biomass feedstock on
 11 19 or after January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5172HV (1) 86
       mm/sc
  8 11 allowed under section 15.319.
  8 12    Sec. 11.  TAX CREDIT CLAIMS.  Renewable chemical production
  8 13 tax credits issued pursuant to the renewable chemical
  8 14 production tax credit program enacted in this division of this
  8 15 Act shall not be issued by the economic development authority
  8 16 prior to July 1, 2018, and shall not be claimed by a taxpayer
  8 17 prior to September 1, 2018.
  8 18    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  8 19 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  8 20 enactment.
  8 21    Sec. 13.  APPLICABILITY.  This division of this Act applies
  8 22 to renewable chemicals produced in the state from biomass
  8 23 feedstock on or after January 1, 2017.

 11  4 of $10 million per fiscal year is reached.  If the amount of
 11  5 tax credits exceeds this amount in a fiscal year, the EDA
 11  6 is required to establish a wait list and give priority in
 11  7 subsequent years to the eligible businesses on the wait list.
 11  8    The division provides for the confidentiality of certain
 11  9 information under the program.  The identity of a tax credit
 11 10 recipient and the amount of the tax credit shall be considered
 11 11 public information under Code chapter 22 (examination of public
 11 12 records), but any other information or record in the possession
 11 13 of the EDA with respect to the program shall be presumed by
 11 14 the EDA to be a trade secret protected under Code chapter 550
 11 15 or common law and shall be kept confidential by the EDA unless
 11 16 otherwise ordered by a court.
 11 17    The division takes effect upon enactment and applies to
 11 18 renewable chemicals produced in Iowa from biomass feedstock on
 11 19 or after January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5172HV (1) 86
       mm/sc
  8 13 tax credits issued pursuant to the renewable chemical
  8 14 production tax credit program enacted in this division of this
  8 15 Act shall not be issued by the economic development authority
  8 16 prior to July 1, 2018, and shall not be claimed by a taxpayer
  8 17 prior to September 1, 2018.
  8 18    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  8 19 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  8 20 enactment.
  8 21    Sec. 13.  APPLICABILITY.  This division of this Act applies
  8 22 to renewable chemicals produced in the state from biomass
  8 23 feedstock on or after January 1, 2017.
  8 24                           EXPLANATION
  8 25 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 26 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 27    This bill relates to the administration of programs by
  8 28 the economic development authority (EDA) by modifying the
  8 29 high quality jobs program and creating a renewable chemical
  8 30 production tax credit program.
  8 31    DIVISION I ==== HIGH QUALITY JOBS PROGRAM.  Division I limits
  8 32 for a period of five fiscal years the amount of tax credits
  8 33 that may be allocated to the high quality jobs program, which
  8 34 under current law is subject to EDA's maximum aggregate tax
  8 35 credit cap of $170 million per fiscal year in Code section
  9  1 15.119.  The bill provides that for each of the five fiscal
  9  2 years beginning on July 1, 2016, and ending on June 30, 2021,
  9  3 the authority shall not allocate more than $105 million of
  9  4 that $170 million cap to the high quality jobs program.  This
  9  5 provision is repealed July 1, 2021.
  9  6    DIVISION II ==== RENEWABLE CHEMICAL PRODUCTION TAX CREDIT.
  9  7   Division II creates a renewable chemical production tax credit
  9  8 program (program) that will be administered by the EDA and that
  9  9 will provide tax credits to eligible businesses that produce
  9 10 renewable chemicals in Iowa from biomass feedstock.  "Renewable
  9 11 chemical", "biomass feedstock", and other related terms are
  9 12 defined in the division.
  9 13    In order to qualify for the tax credit, a business must
  9 14 meet several requirements.  First, the business must be
  9 15 physically located in Iowa and operated for profit under
  9 16 single management.  Second, the business must not be an
  9 17 entity providing professional services, health care services,
  9 18 or medical treatments, or be engaged primarily in retail
  9 19 operations.  Third, the business must have organized, expanded,
  9 20 or located in Iowa on or after the effective date of the
  9 21 division.  Fourth, the business must not be, in the discretion
  9 22 of the EDA, ineligible under certain provisions relating to the
  9 23 relocation or reduction of business operations within Iowa.
  9 24 Fifth, the business must be in compliance with all agreements
  9 25 entered into under the program or other programs administered
  9 26 by the EDA.
  9 27    An eligible business seeking a tax credit is required to
  9 28 submit an application to the EDA containing various information
  9 29 during the calendar year following the calendar year in which
  9 30 the renewable chemicals are produced. The EDA may accept
  9 31 applications on a continuous basis or may establish an annual
  9 32 application deadline.
  9 33    Before being issued a tax credit, an eligible business
  9 34 is required to enter into an agreement with the EDA for the
  9 35 successful completion of all requirements of the program.  The
 10  1 EDA is authorized to impose two compliance cost fees under the
 10  2 program.  The first fee equals $500 per agreement.  The second
 10  3 fee equals 0.5 percent of the value of the tax credit claimed
 10  4 pursuant to the agreement if the agreement has an aggregate tax
 10  5 credit value of $100,000 or greater.
 10  6    An eligible business that fails to comply with the
 10  7 requirements of the program or the terms of an agreement with
 10  8 the EDA may have its tax credits reduced, terminated, or
 10  9 rescinded, and may be subject to the repayment or recapture of
 10 10 claimed tax credits.
 10 11    The tax credit equals the product of $.05 multiplied by the
 10 12 number of pounds of renewable chemicals produced in Iowa from
 10 13 biomass feedstock by the eligible business during the calendar
 10 14 year.  Renewable chemicals produced by an eligible business
 10 15 either prior to calendar year 2017 or prior to the date the
 10 16 business first qualifies as an eligible business, or after
 10 17 calendar year 2027, shall not qualify for the tax credit.
 10 18    The tax credit shall be claimed for the tax year during which
 10 19 the eligible business was issued the tax credit.  However, tax
 10 20 credits shall not be issued by EDA prior to July 1, 2018, or
 10 21 claimed by the taxpayer prior to September 1, 2018. The tax
 10 22 credit may be claimed against the individual income tax and the
 10 23 corporate income tax.  The credit is refundable or may, at the
 10 24 election of the taxpayer, be carried forward for up to one tax
 10 25 year.   The tax credit shall not be transferred to any person.
 10 26    The division provides that the program is subject to EDA's
 10 27 maximum aggregate tax credit cap of $170 million per fiscal
 10 28 year in Code section 15.119, and not more than $10 million
 10 29 per fiscal year may be issued by the EDA under the program.
 10 30 In addition, the maximum amount of tax credit that may be
 10 31 issued to an eligible business for the production of renewable
 10 32 chemicals in any one calendar year shall not exceed $1 million
 10 33 or $500,000, depending on whether the eligible business has
 10 34 been operating in Iowa at the time of application for five
 10 35 or fewer years, or more than five years, respectively.  An
 11  1 eligible business shall not receive more than five tax credits
 11  2 under the program.  The EDA is required to issue tax credits
 11  3 on a first=come, first=served basis until the maximum amount
 11  4 of $10 million per fiscal year is reached.  If the amount of
 11  5 tax credits exceeds this amount in a fiscal year, the EDA
 11  6 is required to establish a wait list and give priority in
 11  7 subsequent years to the eligible businesses on the wait list.
 11  8    The division provides for the confidentiality of certain
 11  9 information under the program.  The identity of a tax credit
 11 10 recipient and the amount of the tax credit shall be considered
 11 11 public information under Code chapter 22 (examination of public
 11 12 records), but any other information or record in the possession
 11 13 of the EDA with respect to the program shall be presumed by
 11 14 the EDA to be a trade secret protected under Code chapter 550
 11 15 or common law and shall be kept confidential by the EDA unless
 11 16 otherwise ordered by a court.
 11 17    The division takes effect upon enactment and applies to
 11 18 renewable chemicals produced in Iowa from biomass feedstock on
 11 19 or after January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5172HV (1) 86
       mm/sc
  8 14 production tax credit program enacted in this division of this
  8 15 Act shall not be issued by the economic development authority
  8 16 prior to July 1, 2018, and shall not be claimed by a taxpayer
  8 17 prior to September 1, 2018.
  8 18    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  8 19 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  8 20 enactment.
  8 21    Sec. 13.  APPLICABILITY.  This division of this Act applies
  8 22 to renewable chemicals produced in the state from biomass
  8 23 feedstock on or after January 1, 2017.

  9 16 single management.  Second, the business must not be an
  9 17 entity providing professional services, health care services,
  9 18 or medical treatments, or be engaged primarily in retail
  9 19 operations.  Third, the business must have organized, expanded,
  9 20 or located in Iowa on or after the effective date of the
  9 21 division.  Fourth, the business must not be, in the discretion
  9 22 of the EDA, ineligible under certain provisions relating to the
  9 23 relocation or reduction of business operations within Iowa.
  9 24 Fifth, the business must be in compliance with all agreements
  9 25 entered into under the program or other programs administered
  9 26 by the EDA.
  9 27    An eligible business seeking a tax credit is required to
  9 28 submit an application to the EDA containing various information
  9 29 during the calendar year following the calendar year in which
  9 30 the renewable chemicals are produced. The EDA may accept
  9 31 applications on a continuous basis or may establish an annual
  9 32 application deadline.
  9 33    Before being issued a tax credit, an eligible business
  9 34 is required to enter into an agreement with the EDA for the
  9 35 successful completion of all requirements of the program.  The
 10  1 EDA is authorized to impose two compliance cost fees under the
 10  2 program.  The first fee equals $500 per agreement.  The second
 10  3 fee equals 0.5 percent of the value of the tax credit claimed
 10  4 pursuant to the agreement if the agreement has an aggregate tax
 10  5 credit value of $100,000 or greater.
 10  6    An eligible business that fails to comply with the
 10  7 requirements of the program or the terms of an agreement with
 10  8 the EDA may have its tax credits reduced, terminated, or
 10  9 rescinded, and may be subject to the repayment or recapture of
 10 10 claimed tax credits.
 10 11    The tax credit equals the product of $.05 multiplied by the
 10 12 number of pounds of renewable chemicals produced in Iowa from
 10 13 biomass feedstock by the eligible business during the calendar
 10 14 year.  Renewable chemicals produced by an eligible business
 10 15 either prior to calendar year 2017 or prior to the date the
 10 16 business first qualifies as an eligible business, or after
 10 17 calendar year 2027, shall not qualify for the tax credit.
 10 18    The tax credit shall be claimed for the tax year during which
 10 19 the eligible business was issued the tax credit.  However, tax
 10 20 credits shall not be issued by EDA prior to July 1, 2018, or
 10 21 claimed by the taxpayer prior to September 1, 2018. The tax
 10 22 credit may be claimed against the individual income tax and the
 10 23 corporate income tax.  The credit is refundable or may, at the
 10 24 election of the taxpayer, be carried forward for up to one tax
 10 25 year.   The tax credit shall not be transferred to any person.
 10 26    The division provides that the program is subject to EDA's
 10 27 maximum aggregate tax credit cap of $170 million per fiscal
 10 28 year in Code section 15.119, and not more than $10 million
 10 29 per fiscal year may be issued by the EDA under the program.
 10 30 In addition, the maximum amount of tax credit that may be
 10 31 issued to an eligible business for the production of renewable
 10 32 chemicals in any one calendar year shall not exceed $1 million
 10 33 or $500,000, depending on whether the eligible business has
 10 34 been operating in Iowa at the time of application for five
 10 35 or fewer years, or more than five years, respectively.  An
 11  1 eligible business shall not receive more than five tax credits
 11  2 under the program.  The EDA is required to issue tax credits
 11  3 on a first=come, first=served basis until the maximum amount
 11  4 of $10 million per fiscal year is reached.  If the amount of
 11  5 tax credits exceeds this amount in a fiscal year, the EDA
 11  6 is required to establish a wait list and give priority in
 11  7 subsequent years to the eligible businesses on the wait list.
 11  8    The division provides for the confidentiality of certain
 11  9 information under the program.  The identity of a tax credit
 11 10 recipient and the amount of the tax credit shall be considered
 11 11 public information under Code chapter 22 (examination of public
 11 12 records), but any other information or record in the possession
 11 13 of the EDA with respect to the program shall be presumed by
 11 14 the EDA to be a trade secret protected under Code chapter 550
 11 15 or common law and shall be kept confidential by the EDA unless
 11 16 otherwise ordered by a court.
 11 17    The division takes effect upon enactment and applies to
 11 18 renewable chemicals produced in Iowa from biomass feedstock on
 11 19 or after January 1, 2017.
       LSB 5172HV (1) 86
       mm/sc
  8 18    Sec. 12.  EFFECTIVE UPON ENACTMENT.  This division of this
  8 19 Act, being deemed of immediate importance, takes effect upon
  8 20 enactment.
  8 21    Sec. 13.  APPLICABILITY.  This division of this Act applies
  8 22 to renewable chemicals produced in the state from biomass
  8 23 feedstock on or after January 1, 2017.
  8 24                           EXPLANATION
  8 25 The inclusion of this explanation does not constitute agreement with
  8 26 the explanation's substance by the members of the general assembly.
  8 27    This bill relates to the administration of programs by
  8 28 the economic development authority (EDA) by modifying the
  8 29 high quality jobs program and creating a renewable chemical
  8 30 production tax credit program.
  8 31    DIVISION I ==== HIGH QUALITY JOBS PROGRAM.  Division I limits
  8 32 for a period of five fiscal years the amount of tax credits
  8 33 that may be allocated to the high quality jobs program, which
  8 34 under current law is subject to EDA's maximum aggregate tax
  8 35 credit cap of $170 million per fiscal year in Code section
  9  1 15.119.  The bill provides that for each of the five fiscal
  9  2 years beginning on July 1, 2016, and ending on June 30, 2021,
  9  3 the authority shall not allocate more than $105 million of
  9  4 that $170 million cap to the high quality jobs program.  This
  9  5 provision is repealed July 1, 2021.
  9  6    DIVISION II ==== RENEWABLE CHEMICAL PRODUCTION TAX CREDIT.
  9  7   Division II creates a renewable chemical production tax credit
  9  8 program (program) that will be administered by the EDA and that
  9  9 will provide tax credits to eligible businesses that produce
  9 10 renewable chemicals in Iowa from biomass feedstock.  "Renewable
  9 11 chemical", "biomass feedstock", and other related terms are
  9 12 defined in the division.
  9 13    In order to qualify for the tax credit, a business must
  9 14 meet several requirements.  First, the business must be
  9 15 physically located in Iowa and operated for profit under
  9 16 single management.  Second, the business must not be an
  9 17 entity providing professional services, health care services,
  9 18 or medical treatments, or be engaged primarily in retail
  9 19 operations.  Third, the business must have organized, expanded,
  9 20 or located in Iowa on or after the effective date of the
  9 21 division.  Fourth, the business must not be, in the discretion
  9 22 of the EDA, ineligible under certain provisions relating to the
  9 23 relocation or reduction of business operations within Iowa.
  9 24 Fifth, the business must be in compliance with all agreements
  9 25 entered into under the program or other programs administered
  9 26 by the EDA.

  9 28 submit an application to the EDA containing various information

  9 31 applications on a continuous basis or may establish an annual
  9 32 application deadline.

 10  5 credit value of $100,000 or greater.

 10  8 the EDA may have its tax credits reduced, terminated, or
 10  9 rescinded, and may be subject to the repayment or recapture of
 10 10 claimed tax credits.
 10 11    The tax credit equals the product of $.05 multiplied by the
 10 12 number of pounds of renewable chemicals produced in Iowa from
 10 13 biomass feedstock by the eligible business during the calendar
 10 14 year.  Renewable chemicals produced by an eligible business
 10 15 either prior to calendar year 2017 or prior to the date the
 10 16 business first qualifies as an eligible business, or after
 10 17 calendar year 2027, shall not qualify for the tax credit.
 10 18    The tax credit shall be claimed for the tax year during which
 10 19 the eligible business was issued the tax credit.  However, tax
 10 20 credits shall not be issued by EDA prior to July 1, 2018, or
 10 21 claimed by the taxpayer prior to September 1, 2018. The tax
 10 22 credit may be claimed against the individual income tax and the
 10 23 corporate income tax.  The credit is refundable or may, at the
 10 24 election of the taxpayer, be carried forward for up to one tax
 10 25 year.   The tax credit shall not be transferred to any person.

 11  5 tax credits exceeds this amount in a fiscal year, the EDA
